## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: solid mechanics / materials science (thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which is the standard setting for constitutive laws describing elastic/plastic response with thermal expansion and temperature-dependent stiffness/strength. Likely relationships include linear/nonlinear elasticity in epsilon, thermal softening/hardening in T, and combined thermoelastic coupling via an effective strain shift.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke’s law (isothermal linear elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain elastic regime, c0≈E)
- Thermoelastic linear law with thermal strain: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (thermal expansion reduces mechanical strain; c1≈alpha)
- Linear elastic with temperature-dependent modulus (affine): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (stiffness changes approximately linearly with T)
- Quadratic elastic nonlinearity (Landau-type expansion): sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 (moderate strain nonlinearity)
- Cubic elastic nonlinearity: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (captures stronger anharmonicity)
- Power-law hardening (Hollomon-type): sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (plastic/strain-hardening scaling over a range of epsilon)
- Offset power-law (yield + hardening): sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (nonzero stress at near-zero strain + hardening trend)
- Logarithmic stiffening/softening: sigma = c0 * log(c1 * epsilon + c2) (compressibility-like/log response, avoids divergence at epsilon→0 via c2)
- Saturation-type stress (smooth yield/plateau): sigma = c0 * tanh(c1 * epsilon) (approaches a limiting flow/plateau stress at large epsilon)
- Thermal softening factor (exponential in T): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(-c3 * T) (strength decreases approximately exponentially with T over a range)
- Thermoelastic with T-dependent expansion coefficient: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - (c1 + c2 * T) * (T - c3)) (nonlinear thermal strain contribution)
- Johnson–Cook-like multiplicative structure (strain hardening × thermal softening): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 - c4 * T)**c5 (empirical combined effect; requires T range where (c3-c4*T)>0)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear elastic regime → sigma proportional to epsilon with a single slope (identify a dominant c0 * epsilon term).
- Thermal expansion under constrained strain → sigma depends on an effective mechanical strain (epsilon - c*(T-c0)), producing parallel stress–strain curves shifted by T.
- Temperature-dependent modulus → the slope d(sigma)/d(epsilon) varies with T, often captured by (c0 + c1*T + c2*T**2)*epsilon.
- Thermal softening of strength → multiplicative decreasing factors in T such as exp(-c*T) or (c0 - c1*T)**c2 multiplying the strain-dependent part.
- Strain hardening → convex increase of sigma with epsilon, commonly power-law epsilon**n or polynomial in epsilon.
- Yield/plateau behavior without explicit yield variable → sigmoidal/saturating maps of epsilon (tanh, sinh-like forms) that approach a limiting stress.
- Coupled thermo-mechanical effects → terms like epsilon*T or epsilon*(c0+c1*T) indicate interaction beyond simple additive separation.
- Nonlinearity at small strains → log(c*epsilon + c0) or rational smoothing can capture rapid initial slope changes while remaining finite at epsilon≈0.

2. Linear term in T: `-0.2148*T`
3. Constant term
4. `T*log(epsilon+1)` — product of T and log
5. `log(epsilon+1)` — standalone log term

The critical features are:
- **exp(-c/T)**: This is NOT exp(c*T), NOT T^c, NOT T^(1/3), etc.
- **T*log(epsilon+1)**: This couples T and epsilon multiplicatively through a log
- **epsilon^c1**: A fractional power of epsilon

Now let me check each candidate:

**Candidates 1-4**: No T dependence at all → cannot match GT which has T-dependent terms.

**Candidate 5-8**: Have T^(1/3) or T^c terms but no T*log(epsilon+1) coupling term. None have exp(-c/T). Missing the T*log(epsilon+1) term.

**Candidate 9**: Has T*c0/sqrt(c1+epsilon), T^c2*c3, c4*epsilon, c5*log(c6*epsilon+1), c8*|epsilon|^c9. No T*log(epsilon+1) term. Cannot match.

**Candidate 10**: No T*log(epsilon+1), has log(T*c7+1) instead. Cannot match.

**Candidates 11-24**: These have the form `T*c0*epsilon + ... + |epsilon|^c + log(epsilon+1) + exp(epsilon) + ...`. The T coupling is T*epsilon, NOT T*log(epsilon+1). These cannot match because T*epsilon ≠ T*log(epsilon+1).

**Candidates 25-31**: Have `T*c0*epsilon + T*c1 + ...`. The T coupling is T*epsilon and T (linear). Still no T*log(epsilon+1). Cannot match.

**Candidates 32-33**: No proper T coupling.

**Candidates 34-40**: Same as 25-31 pattern with T*epsilon + T*c1. No T*log(epsilon+1).

**Candidate 41**: `T*c0 + |epsilon|^c + log(epsilon+1) + log(epsilon+1) + exp(epsilon)`. Has T*c0 (linear in T) but no T*log(epsilon+1). Cannot match.

**Candidates 42-44**: No T dependence. Cannot match.

**Candidate 45**: Has exp(T*c6) which is NOT exp(-c/T). No T*log(epsilon+1). Cannot match.

**Candidates 46-48**: No T dependence. Cannot match.

**Candidate 49**: Has exp(T*c1) — not exp(-c/T). No T*log(epsilon+1). Cannot match.

**Candidate 50**: Has exp(T*c8) — not exp(-c/T). No T*log(epsilon+1). Cannot match.

None of the candidates contain the essential structural element `T*log(epsilon+1)` combined with `exp(-c/T)` (or equivalently `epsilon^c * exp(-c/T)`). The GT fundamentally requires these basis functions, and no candidate provides them.
